<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">This paper presents a robust spur reduction technique using a switched-capacitor feedback differential phase-locked loop (PLL) and a delay-locked-loop (DLL)-based spread-spectrum clock generation in a UHF-band RF identification transmitter (TX). The proposed differential PLL is characterized by adopting a switched-capacitor common-mode feedback and distributed varactor biasing scheme to the differential charge pump and voltage-controlled oscillator designs, respectively, which results in down to 94 dBc in reference spur rejection with all digital parts off. Additionally, by adopting an 8-bit DLL and Hershey-Kiss modulated profile together, the proposed spread-spectrum clock generator shows more than 20-dB electromagnetic-interference reduction while providing up-, down-, and center-spread modes. Implemented in a 0.18m CMOS process, the proposed TX achieves &lt;; - 80-dBc spur suppression with 25-dBm transmit power at 920 MHz, which complies with the most stringent regulatory spectral mask without a surface acoustic wave filter.</div>

Transmitter&quot;,&quot;rightsLink&quot;:&quot;http://s100.copyright.com/AppDispatchServlet?publisherName=ieee&amp;publication=&amp;title=Spur+Reduction+Techniques+With+a+Switched-Capacitor+Feedback+Differential+PLL+and+a+DLL-Based+SSCG+in+UHF+RFID+Transmitter&amp;isbn=&amp;publicationDate=&amp;author=&amp;ContentID=&amp;orderBeanReset=true&quot;,&quot;pubLink&quot;:&quot;/xpl/RecentIssue.jsp?punumber=22&quot;,&quot;issueLink&quot;:&quot;/xpl/tocresult.jsp?isnumber=null&quot;,&quot;standardTitle&quot;:&quot;Spur <div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>As the demand for fully integrated system-on-chip (SoC) solutions continues to grow, there has been increased interest in the analog/digital coexistence issue in relation to system design. Although SoC generally offers advantages of lower power and cost compared to multi-chip solutions, it inevitably suffers from radiated electromagnetic interference (EMI) due to digital switching noise. The EMI is prone to turn into spurious single tones at the harmonic frequencies of the clock signal, and consequently threatens the reliability of data processing in RF and analog circuits in the wireless transceiver. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7078974/7051289/7051289-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7078974/7051289/7051289-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>Spectrum mask in ARIB-t107 standard.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7051289/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
describes the spectrum mask in an ARIB-T107 standard set by regulatory agencies from Japan, which has the most stringent specification requirements of UHF band RF identification (RFID) applications; i.e., a spur level of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 3.426em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.066em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.01em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-3"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-4"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-5" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">&lt;</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-6" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">−</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-7" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-8"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-9"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-10"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-11" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">79</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.13em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">{&lt;} -{\hbox{79}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> dBc with 24-dBm transmit power <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>. To satisfy this specification, spur rejection in the analog part of the SoC is required, as well as that from EMI in the digital part. In general, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>, the reference spur at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-12" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.9em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-13"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-14"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-15" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-16"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-17"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-18" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and digital switching spur at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-19" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.38em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-20"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-21" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-22"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-23" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-24"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-25"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-26" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">2f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are the most crucial factor violating the spectral mask requirement in wireless transceiver design. In order to overcome this spur issue, most industrial RFID transmitters (TXs) are accompanied by external components such as surface acoustic wave (SAW) filters. However, the external SAW filter increases manufacturing and assembly costs. In order to suppress the reference spur at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-27" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.9em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-28"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-29"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-30" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-31"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-32"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-33" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> without SAW filters the differential phase-locked loops (PLLs) are widely used. In a differential phase-locked loop (DPLL), the op-amp based common-mode feedback (CMFB) is preferred to reduce up/down current mismatch in the charge pump (CP) that is one of the main causes of the reference spur <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. However, even if the op-amp-based CMFB mitigates up/down current mismatch, differential error in the DPLL still needs to be resolved <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>. Meanwhile, as a simple and straightforward solution to alleviate the EMI, a spread-spectrum clock generator (SSCG) has been reported <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>. An SSCG varies the clock frequency with continuous up/down modulation, thus decentralizing the concentrated spectrum such that the radiated power level in a given bandwidth is reduced. In our previous work <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>, the SSCG based on a delay-locked loop (DLL) was proposed for EMI reduction and manifested its effectiveness satisfying the ARIB-T107 spectrum mask. However, since reduction of the reference spur in the PLL is also significant, the explanation how to reduce the reference spur should have been discussed in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>. In this paper, a spur reduction technique for a 920-MHz UHF-band RFID TX using a switched-capacitor common-mode feedback differential phase-locked loop (SC-CMFB PLL) in addition to the DLL-based SSCG is presented. The TX complies with the UHF-band RFID spectral mask specification without requiring a SAW filter. In the proposed PLL, the differential CP minimizes differential errors by adopting SC-CMFB, while the op-amp-based CMFB helps to match its up/down current. The main advantages of SC-CMFBs are that they impose no restrictions on the maximum allowable differential input signals, have no additional parasitic poles in the CM loop, and are highly linear <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>. Additionally, contrary to the structures utilizing op-amps or other active circuits <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>, SC-CMFB has benefits in the aspects of power consumption, design complexity, and loop stability since it is all composed of passive elements such as capacitors and switches. Moreover, the distributed varactor biasing scheme <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a> is adopted in the differential voltage-controlled oscillator (VCO) for better spur rejection through more linearized and differential tuning curve. Apart from the spur reduction in analog part of the TX, the SSCG helps to reduce EMI from digital switching noise. The proposed SSCG is implemented with a direct digital phase domain modulation (DDPM) scheme along with a 256 phase generator, an 8-bit DLL, and a Hershey-Kiss (H-K) profile generator, and thereby provides robust EMI reduction in conjunction with area efficiency. This paper is organized as follows. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Sections II</a> and <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">III</a> depict the TX architecture and SC-CMFB DPLL, respectively. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Sections IV</a> and <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5" class="fulltext-link">V</a> describe operating principle and implementation details of the proposed SSCG. Finally, <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec6" class="fulltext-link">Section VI</a> presents experimental results and <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec7" class="fulltext-link">Section VII</a> concludes this paper.<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>TX Architecture</h2></div><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a> presents a block diagram of the presented RFID TX. As shown in the figure, the TX adopts a mixer based direct conversion architecture that consists of a baseband modem, a 9-bit digital-to-analog converter (DAC), a low-pass filter (LPF) for channel selection, an up-mixer, and a driving amp (DA) along with an external power amp (PA) that amplifies signals to a level appropriate for transmission (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-34" role="math" style="width: 2.045em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.805em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1001.75em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-35"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-36"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-37"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-38" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">&gt;</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-39"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-40"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-41"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-42"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-43" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">25</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.13em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">{&gt;}{\hbox{25}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> dBm). The TX is designed to satisfy the spur specification at 25-dBm PA output power in ARIB-T107 by utilizing a DPLL and SSCG. For ARIB-T107 specification, the spurs from both the PLL reference clock in the analog part and EMI in the digital part should be considered simultaneously. For the spur rejection in the analog part, a DPLL is adopted, while a DLL-based SSCG suppresses the spurs from EMI in the digital part. The proposed DPLL is characterized by the structures of the differential CP using SC-CMFB and the differential VCO with linearized tuning curves. The SC-CMFB-based CP reduces its differential errors without extra power consumption or stability issues by using only passive elements, while the conventional CPs utilize active circuits including op-amps. Besides, the distributed varactor biasing scheme is adopted in VCO design, which linearizes the frequency tuning curves. This facilitates the design of differential tuning curves in the VCO to be more accurate and thereby optimizes the spur rejection performance of the DPLL. Contrary to the conventional SSCG, the proposed SSCG is designed based on the DLL and suppresses the spurs at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-44" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.38em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-45"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-46" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-47"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-48" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-49"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-50"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-51" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-6">2f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> by reducing EMI in the digital part of the SoC through the H-K modulation profile <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_2">[5]</a>. Since the switching clock in SC-CMFB circuits and the operating clock in the SSCG share the reference clock of the PLL, an additional clock generation is unnecessary.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7078974/7051289/7051289-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7078974/7051289/7051289-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig><p>TX architecture.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7051289/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7078974/7051289/7051289-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7078974/7051289/7051289-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3. </b><fig><p>Architecture and operating principle of DPLL.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7051289/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>DPLL Utilizing SC-CMFB CP</h2></div><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a> shows the block diagram and operating principle of the proposed DPLL. As seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>, the proposed DPLL is comprised of a tri-state phase-frequency detector (PFD), an SC-CMFB differential CP, a loop filter (LF), a differential VCO, and frequency dividers. A delta–sigma modulator (DSM) is not depicted in the figure, but digitally integrated. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a> shows the operating principle of the DPLL. A DPLL suppresses the reference spurs, caused by CP differential errors or directly passed through supply paths, by designing VCO tuning curves in a differential configuration. For a better spur rejection, as seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>, the control voltages of the differential VCO, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-7-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-52" role="math" style="width: 3.727em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.366em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.37em 2.646em -999.997em); height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-56"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-57"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-58"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-59"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-60" style="font-size: 70.7%; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-70"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-71"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-72"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-73"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-74" style="font-size: 70.7%; For this, the differential errors in the CP have to be reduced in advance. According to <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_3">[2]</a>, the amount of the reference spur in the PLL, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-12-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-116" role="math" style="width: 1.805em; top: -5.102em; left: 0.003em; width: 100%;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-125"><span class="mtable" id="MathJax-Span-126" style="min-width: 27.691em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 100%; height: 0px; min-width: 27.691em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: absolute; width: 23.486em; height: 0px; clip: rect(-2.459em 1023.49em 1.985em -999.997em); top: 0.003em; left: 50%; As seen in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1" href="#deqn1" class="fulltext-link">(1)</a>, in order to reduce the reference spurs, it is helpful to decrease the CP current, VCO gain, and the pole frequency of the LF or increase the reference frequency. However, the increase of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-273" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.9em 2.526em -999.997em); overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-20">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is not desirable due to the cost of XTAL and EMI increase, while the decrease in <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-21-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-280" role="math" style="width: 1.685em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.5em 2.526em -999.997em); clip: rect(3.186em 1000.48em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-283" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">I<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.345em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1002.35em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-289"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-290"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.345em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-291" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-292"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-293"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-294" style="font-size: 70.7%; On the other hand, since a decrease in <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-300" role="math" style="width: 2.826em; top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-301"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-302"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.526em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.9em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-303" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">K<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-304"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-305"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-306" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">O</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-23">K_{\rm VCO}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is desirable in phase-noise performance, it can be beneficial to realize spur rejection by using a multi-bit capacitor bank in the VCO design. The proposed PLL is characterized by the structures of the differential CP and VCO. The proposed CP is designed utilizing an op-amp-based up/down current matching technique <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_3">[2]</a> and minimizes its differential errors by adopting SC-CMFB. The differential VCO is basically designed in a differential varactor structure where each varactor cell is more linearized by distributed varactor biasing scheme <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_3">[8]</a>. This linearization allows the differential frequency tuning curves to be more symmetrical regardless of the control voltage of the VCO.<p></p><div class="section_2" id="sec3a"><h3>A. SC-CMFB Differential CP</h3><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a> describes the schematic of SC-CMFB circuits and its modeling for principle understanding. As seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-24-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-309" role="math" style="width: 2.105em; Therefore, it is evident that the output common-mode sensing and comparison are achieved <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_3a">[7]</a>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a> shows the schematic of the proposed differential CP. Based on the op-amp CMFB, the up/down currents are matched regardless of output voltage variation. As mentioned earlier, SC-CMFB is utilized to minimize differential error without additional power consumption and stability issues. Since the VCO is designed to have the center point of its tuning curve at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-711" role="math" style="width: 3.126em; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-727"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-728"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-729" style="font-size: 70.7%; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-731"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-732"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-733" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-734" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">V_{DD}/2</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Therefore, during the first phase <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-735" role="math" style="width: 1.264em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.14em 2.465em -999.997em); clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-738" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Φ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-739"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-740"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-741" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-39">\Phi_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the voltage, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-40-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-742" role="math" style="width: 7.09em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.369em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1006.37em 2.706em -999.997em); font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">D</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-749" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">D</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-750"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-751"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-752" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-753" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-754" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">−</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-755" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.285em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-756" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">B</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-760" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-761" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-40">V_{DD}/2 - V_{B,P1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, is charged to the capacitor and finally generates the proper CMFB voltage, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-763" role="math" style="width: 2.045em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.805em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.8em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-764"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-765"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.805em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-766" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-767"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-768"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-769" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-770" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">M</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.68em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-772"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-773"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-774" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-775"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-776"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-777" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">D</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-778" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">V_{\rm DC}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. For switching in the SC-CMFB circuit, the reference clock of the PLL is co-used without additional clock generation. Since the bandwidth of the LF is set to 10 kHz, 19.2 MHz of the reference clock does not degrade spur characteristics.

<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3b"><h3>B. Differential VCO With Distributed Varactor Biasing</h3><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7078974/7051289/7051289-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7078974/7051289/7051289-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>VCO structure with distributed varactor biasing.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7051289/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7(a)</a> describes the schematic of the differential VCO. The VCO is basically designed in an nMOSFET-only structure with inductive source degeneration. In the resonator design, a symmetrical spiral inductor and 6-bit capacitor bank are used. For reference spur rejection, as well as common-mode noise suppression, we utilize differentially tuned varactors where the distributed varactors are biased independently to have more linear frequency tuning curve. For a given frequency tuning range, a single varactor presents a relatively higher VCO gain <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-779" role="math" style="width: 3.667em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.306em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.19em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-780"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-781" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-782"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.526em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.9em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-783" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">K<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-784"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-785"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-786" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">V</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-787" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-788" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">O</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-789" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-43">(K_{\rm VCO})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> variation up to the control voltage and further nonlinear tuning curve than those of the distributed varactor biasing scheme. An excessive variation in <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-44-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-790" role="math" style="width: 2.826em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.526em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.53em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-791"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-792"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.526em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.9em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-793" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">K<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-794"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-795"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-796" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">V</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-797" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-798" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">O</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-44">K_{\rm VCO}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> causes PLL loop gain variation and finally leads to PLL stability issues. In addition, nonlinear <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-45-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-799" role="math" style="width: 2.826em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.526em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.53em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-800"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-801"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.526em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.9em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-802" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">K<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-803"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-804"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-805" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">V</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-806" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-807" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">O</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-45">K_{\rm VCO}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> disturbs the differential configuration of frequency tuning curves in VCOs. Since the differential error reduction in <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-46-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-808" role="math" style="width: 2.826em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.526em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.53em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-809"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-810"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.526em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.9em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-811" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">K<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-812"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-813"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-814" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">V</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-815" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-816" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">O</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-46">K_{\rm VCO}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is also as important as that in the CP for reference spur rejection, the linearization of the tuning curve is significant. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a> is the principle of the distributed varactor biasing scheme. As seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>, each of the varactors in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7(a)</a> is biased to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-47-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-817" role="math" style="width: 1.745em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.57em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-818"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-819"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-820" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.183em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-821"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-822"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-823" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">B</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-824" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-47">V_{B1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-825" role="math" style="width: 1.745em; top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-826"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-827"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-49">V_{B3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, respectively, and thereby the corresponding tuning curves are shifted so that the total capacitance variation up to the control voltage becomes more linear. The combination of differential error minimization in the CP and VCO tuning curves eventually results in reference spur rejection. The design parameters including

Frequency Dividers and LF</h3><p>The frequency dividers in the feed-through path and in the feed-back path in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a> are designed in current-mode-logic (CML) and dual modulus types, respectively. The LF is basically designed in second order, but one more <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-850" role="math" style="width: 0.904em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.784em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.78em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-851"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-852" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-51">R</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-52-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-853" role="math" style="width: 0.904em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.784em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.78em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-854"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-855" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-52">C</script></tex-math></inline-formula> network is added to further suppress the reference spur. For 10 kHz or there about PLL bandwidth, the external passive elements are used, except <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-53-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-856" role="math" style="width: 1.324em; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-859" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-860"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-861"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-862" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-53">R_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-54-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-863" role="math" style="width: 1.264em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.14em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-864"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-865"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-866" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-867"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-868"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-869" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-54">C_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The passive element values of the LF in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a> are summarized in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">Table II</a>.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Principle of DDPM in SSCG</h2></div><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a> shows the operating principle of the DDPM scheme. As seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a>, the DDPM allows to achieve spread-spectrum function by shuffling the multiple equi-spacing <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-870" role="math" style="width: 2.646em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.345em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.23em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-871"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-872" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-873" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-874" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">T<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-875" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-55">(\Delta T)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> delay taps with a phase-modulated multiplexer (MUX) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_4">[4]</a>. Even though the DDPM scheme has benefits in area and power aspects by eliminating the use of the bulky PLL, it requires an infinite number of phases owing to its inherent characteristic of phase modulation. As can be seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>, since the phase is persistently accumulated, the phase modulation can be extended to infinity in the time domain while the frequency modulation <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-876" role="math" style="width: 3.426em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.066em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.95em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-877"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-878" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-879"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.285em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-880" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-881"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-882"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-883" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">M</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-884" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">O</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-885" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">D</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-886" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-56">(f_{\rm MOD})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> keeps changing up and down within a limited boundary. In order to realize an infinite number of phases, a phase-wrapping technique was developed in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_4">[4]</a>. This technique utilized a finite number of delay cells instead of an infinite number of delay cells, where the wrap-around is done moving back by the number of taps per period. However, as the calibration logic operates adjusting the number of delay cells rather than the amount of delay, this technique raises the digital processing complexity as well as requires additional peripheral circuits such as clock edge monitoring modules and delay compensators. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_4">[6]</a>, we proposed a DLL-based phase-calibration technique that adjusts the amount of the unit cell delay allowing spread-spectrum function with a limited number of delay cells. In the proposed technique, the digital processing complexity can be alleviated by deciding the number of delay cells in a binary manner, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-887" role="math" style="width: 1.324em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.084em 1001.2em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-888"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-889"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.42em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-890" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.441em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-891"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-892"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-893" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">N<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-57">2^{N}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Moreover, it does not require any clock monitoring circuit due to its inherent recursive phase properties. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10</a> shows the conceptual timing diagram of the proposed DLL-based delay calibration algorithm. As seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a>, in case of using an 8-bit delay, the last phase <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-58-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-894" role="math" style="width: 3.066em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.766em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.65em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-895"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-896" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-897"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.985em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-898" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">D</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-899"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-900"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-901" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">256</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-902" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-58">(D_{256})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is folded to the first phase <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-59-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-903" role="math" style="width: 2.285em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.045em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.92em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-904"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-905" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-906"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-907" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">D</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-908"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-909"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-910" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-911" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-59">(D_{0})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> by maintaining the total delay equal to the clock period. In the proposed DLL, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-60-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-912" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.26em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-913"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-914"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-915" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">D</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-916"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-917"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-918" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-60">D_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-61-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-919" role="math" style="width: 2.225em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.985em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.99em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-920"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-921"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.985em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-922" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">D</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-923"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-924"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-925" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">256</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-61">D_{256}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are compared to make an order to control the subsequent 8-bit digital logic. Thus, the delay amount, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-62-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-926" role="math" style="width: 1.745em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.57em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-927"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-928" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-929" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">T<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-62">\Delta T</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, is calibrated to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-63-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-930" role="math" style="width: 4.628em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.147em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.09em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-931"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-932"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.165em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-933" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">T<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-934"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-935"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-936" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-937" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">L</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-938" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">K</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-939"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-940"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-941" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-942" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">256</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-63">T_{\rm CLK}/256</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and leads to seamless phase continuity in spite of PVT variation and different operating conditions.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7078974/7051289/7051289-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7078974/7051289/7051289-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 9. </b><fig><p>Operating principle of DDPM scheme.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7051289/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
